O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the medical science together with its content, and I have made the end by its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is discouraged in our region and is entirely foreign, the science has been lost and diminished, and nothing remains of its essence except for small descriptions in books by the ancients that the practitioners have moved forward.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came the errors and vanity, and intentions were closed off and the science was distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I should revive it together with the regulation of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of cautery instruments, and other tools of the work along with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of the craft in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who engages in it must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know correctly about the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews and the number of them, and the movement and resting of veins, and their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, should guard against falling into error and harming people; thus I have seen many times those who meddle in this science and rely on their own knowledge and lack of experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a mad doctor who lanced an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut into the arteries of her neck; because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who tried to remove a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut into it he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another doctor who took care of the duke of our land who had his leg broken, and along with the break there was a wound; and the doctors, full of ignorance, set the fracture over the wound with splints very tightly, and left no cloth for the wound at all, and kept it like that; and commanded him not to loosen it; and remained in such a state that the leg became completely swollen and the foot, leading to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and hurried to come and loosen the leg; and when I had loosened it, he felt at ease and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But once corruption had already set in the limb, it could not be cured; and the corruption continued to spread throughout the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another doctor who drained the embedded abscess and then burned it with the malice of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a sore, when it is full of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place where all the corrupted matter can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for that reason, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two categories: namely, work where there is danger in many situations; and I will show in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, it is necessary that you take care so that the foolish doctor cannot speak ill of you. Take your weapons in readiness, and approach your patients lightly but firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you may reach salvation and be praised; and leave behind terrible diseases due to harsh treatment; and remove your weapons from those who cause you doubt, and act in such a way that you may come from this world to the next with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his warnings: "Do not concern yourself with harmful diseases, or you may be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterizations and medicinal hot cauterizations, and the chapter is arranged from head to feet; and on the forms of instruments, and tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping, and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is arranged along with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, as we recall the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of the aid and harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and harm are lengthy speech and subtle science and secret answers; and about this many wise people spoke, and agreed on it; and I suffice with a little of their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the cautery universally aids in every constitution where there is matter, whether it be two constitutions: namely, a hot constitution with matter, and a dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a constitution that is both hot and dry with matter, some argued and said that the cautery is of great help there; and others said the opposite: that the cautery is not useful for diseases coming from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat a hot disease with heat or dryness; and those who say the opposite claim that the cautery provides great help for a hot and dry disease that occurs in the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of the man and his moisture according to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true on occasion through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, let no one interfere except those who have tested it, and who know through long practice the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of temperaments of people, and their predispositions and causes of illnesses, and the outcomes and time intervals; we fear not other temperaments, especially in cold and moist ailments.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors gathered together and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that the fire cautery together is of the secrets of remedies, and of greater goodness than the burning cauterant medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and does not affect any part other than the limb that is being heated, and it does no harm to another limb if one can name it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines spread from one limb to another, causing diseases of difficult healing in the affected member; and by chance they may kill the patient. The fire, due to its height and the goodness of its nature, does not do this, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is upon the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of speech, for it displeases me to take from you the secret which lies in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it removes diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the time when the cauterizations should be performed, and chose appropriate days.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the harmful effects caused can be prevented by the aid of cauterization; and especially if the cauterizations are necessary for pains that cannot wait due to urgency so that no greater harm comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, dear son, as foolish doctors do; for the illness that is cured by cauterization has no relapse; and they say it thus, but they are mistaken because cauterizations are nothing other than medicine that changes the complexion, dries up the humors which cause pain, and is better than medicine for hastening its value, and for the power of its work and sovereignty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the illness comes sometimes according to the constitution of the patient and the place of the disease and its strength; and the excesses are accumulated in him by the consumption of food and similar things, except where there is little excess and moisture, such as cauteries for tooth pain and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort in medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauteries are worth trying after other medicines, yet their understanding is false, for it is cauteries that are the last resort in medicine because when we administer methods of treatment for any illness and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it proves effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterizations with an instrument of gold are better than those with iron, and they said this not because of the quality of the gold or its high substance; but they also said that the skin after cauterization does not become ulcerated, which is not true as I have tested it, and I found that it is true in some people; and cauterizations with gold are indeed better than those with iron, as they claim.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot tell by its color when it is hot enough, and it cools quickly; and if you heat it too much, it becomes damaged by the fire; and thus there are many hindrances.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered this chapter from head to foot, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness affecting the brain, and there are two types made because of a disease called "soda," and due to various humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and for numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and especially for all diseases caused by cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine cleansing the head for three nights or four, according to what the patient's constitution and age can tolerate; and then do behind the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have him sit with his hands between your hands, and place his hands on his thighs; afterwards put the root of your palm at the root of his nose between his two eyes; there where your thumbs will be, let it bleed from there, then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", here is how to make it:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and do by descending and pulling your hand little by little while turning; then lift your hand gradually, and examine the spot if you see a bone slightly protruding; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have said; afterwards take some pitch, put it in wax and soften cotton within, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; then apply moistened cloth in butter; and keep it on until the inflammation is gone; afterwards treat the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmakon", until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and for this reason it helps to move [the patient].
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that one should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that the cautery should be left on for so long and pressed so hard that it cuts into the bone as wide as a quill that women put in their ears to let the humors flow out; and the wound should remain open for a long time afterward; then it must be cleansed and treated.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem entirely good to me, except in some people where there is a danger of fear; and I think I should leave it as such; for the head [of the shoulder] is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other limbs; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, the first appearance of cauterization seems safer and more moderate to me, and from this one I practice with safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain comes to the whole head and lasts for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie," and perform purging of the head and oils and plasters; and if one performs the cautery that we mentioned before, it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the condition of the patient is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold; then cauterize below that area a little as we said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterize each horn of the head up to the bone as we said before, and perform the cautery at the place called "vasselz"; there are places where suction cups are applied; move your hand lightly so you do not see until the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than with others, and I will speak about it later; and the cauterizations of the horns should be finer than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and here is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and spreads up to the eye, and the head is purged with cleansing medicines, and all the other treatments that I have mentioned in the division of diseases have been done, and none of this helps: then I make cauteries according to two methods, namely with dry medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of dry medicine is such that you take a piece of cloth and remove the outer layer and place it in I cup with II chives, and then apply it to the temple where the pain resides in such a manner that you can place the piece of cloth under the skin; and when it is placed there, secure and press it well and leave it so for XII hours; then unbind and treat the wound outside the piece of garlic, and leave the wound like this II days or III; then put on a poultice soaked in butter until it can be removed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to use some burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth chapter on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery of iron is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery as described in its form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bowl with a bit of curvature, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and turn the iron slightly, until half the thickness of the flesh over the heart is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and allow abundant bleeding.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After place cotton in bandage of thread, and put on the site for III days; then put cotton moistened with butter, and then treat the site with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this emigration with the cautery which is called "cultellare", at the entire point, and guard against cutting the artery in this emigration which is not old.
de emigraine	of swelling/inflammation
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat swelling as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and see that the cauterizations previously mentioned from medicine and iron do not suffice for him, then you must heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it becomes white; and cut in this painful place a line half a digit long, and remove your hand once to ensure you do not cut the artery and do not reach the bone; and guard against the jaw that moves when one eats, and the nerve should be cautious so that it does not become mute and spasm does not come upon the patient, and guard against blood loss from the artery when it is cut, or cutting brings great fear even to those who are unfamiliar with it and who have no study and experience; but I will tell you how one stops bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it applies in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations do not help the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on top of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cauterization that we mentioned in the chapter about the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cauterization is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain from coldness comes to the ear, and one has used medicines that dissolve and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "poins," here is its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After puncture all around the diseased ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move away a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place; and put ten points around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the treatment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	A torture that must be treated with a cautery is none other than those that are caused by phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not perform cauterization on similar conditions that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this condition of a phlegm-related torture with purgings and gargling, if that does not suffice, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one at the base of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and the third near the junction of the two lips; place the cautery in an area that appears healthy, and apply it directly above a bit below the horn of the head for the part near the ear, and another at the temple as long as a palm; leave the cauterization on until half the heart is burned; this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is like the example of the knife mentioned before, but it is a bit more subtle and the knife should be a bit larger; after treating the area as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is longstanding and the treatment does not help, and the patient has no fever, then make IV cauterizations: II on the two horns of the head, and I in the middle of the head, and I at the place which is called "vasselz" as we said before, and the last cautery above the stomach; and let them be performed as we have said previously.
de litargie	For litargia (foot ulcer or athlete's
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large doses of iron and purifying pills for the brain; then anoint the head of the patient completely, and place the sinapi plaster on the occiput as described in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is well in this way, it is good; and if not, make III cauterizations between them on the head descending down to the neck, and have I thumb's width of space between each cauterization; and treat as with others, and if you wish to add more, and the patient can bear it, make I cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, II others above the II temples, and treat until he is well; and let the cauterizations which are called «olivare», as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of dirt and what we mentioned before; then anoint the patient's head, then make a cauterization in the middle of the head and above each temple, and one at the back and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient can bear it, and the illness is severe, make four cauterizations on the spine of the back; and leave them until the softest part of the skin is burned, then lift your hand; afterward treat until he is well, and let the cauterizations which are called «olivare» that we mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Those with epilepsy must not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first modify the brain from worms and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is large and suffers greatly from difficult medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot withstand this, give them gargling and chewing to modify the brain frequently with good meat; afterwards raise their head in the middle, and apply the cautery as we have said before, on the vessel and on each temple; and if the patient is strong and suffering, apply cauterizations as I have said for those who have paralysis and limb weakness, on the spine of the back and neck, and let these be olive cauterizations according to the method I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform the delicate cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy the excesses or moister humours are corrupted and phlegm is thick, then apply such cauteries as we have mentioned to one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the excess humours incline towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that purifies the brain, according to what is mentioned before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After elevating the head of the patient; then make a bandage of well-made flax, like a circle, and place it on the head; and have the patient sit cross-legged, held securely from all sides; afterwards apply the poultice, using wool felt from an old sheep; heat it over a gentle fire until it can be comfortably applied to the patient; then empty the circle inside onto the head, and let it cool down; and do this for the patient once every week with other good management, until they are healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you wish to cauterize it, make multiple small punctures across the entire area to be cauterized.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the brain excessively; then apply cotton soaked in butter and goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	from the pain of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When pain first comes to the eyes according to the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something purifying for their head, and protect them from all moistures, and make them sweat in baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterward, command them to lie with their head back, and perform a cauterization in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the pain descends to both eyes together, or one if it is in one; and cut through all veins and arteries that are below the heart throughout the entire cauterization area, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of excessive blood loss, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it as strongly as necessary.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at the incision the caution how you will stop it; and sometimes a cautery or hot iron is applied between the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	from the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins, then treat the arteries that appear on the head's surface; and if you see that it is due to cold phlegmatic excesses, then apply the cautery as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter descending to the eyes: I cautere in the middle of the forehead, and II cauterizations above the two temples, and II cauterizations with a hot iron between the two bones; and if there is further need, cautiously cauterize above the eyebrows with one small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient three nights' worth of drinks; afterward raise his head, and apply a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery; and make two cauterizations called "clavilis" on the two sides, a little below the hair; and be careful of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the white of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to do two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrow hairs are; and do not let go of your hand except when a third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that points toward the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes grow inward and prick the eye, and one performs cauterization according to two methods: namely with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in your care; after that, draw on the paper above the eyes a figure like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then apply cotton moistened with egg white and parsley juice to the eye, then heat the cautery as described here:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure you have drawn little by little many times, so that the skin is burned at those points; and the signs of the work being successful are that you see the paper retract, and the hairs rise to the edge of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave it thus for III days, then apply cotton moistened with butter until the burn has healed; after which treat with ointment until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs come after that, and the skin is softened, then restart the cautery on the same spot as you did before; and if the hairs have fallen out, cauterize until the skin rises to its natural level and becomes even, so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a shape out of parchment like a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and hot vinegar, one ounce each, and grind them together well; and do this quickly so it does not cool down, then sprinkle on the form you have made as with a myrtle leaf, and place over the skin around the eyes; and if the patient has only one affected eye, work on that one alone, but if both are affected, work on both; and place cotton moistened in egg white under the eye of the patient, and press down gently every time the patient feels burning from the medicine, because they will feel it as if it were fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine at its proper time.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the biting has passed, then lift the area of treatment, and examine if you see the skin raised as if it had been raised by the constraint of fire or by cutting; and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply the medicine again to the area where it has not taken effect, until your work is even and your eyes are set properly; then place wet cotton on a piece of butter until the burned area heals, after which treat the ointment application site, known as "diaphanous" and other treatments, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to be very careful with your work so that none of the medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft after that, and the hair pricks in the eye, then reapply the medicine to that place which is softened by the paper properly, as you did before; treat it until it is healed; and this is the form of the mirtle poultice:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of people vary in size and smallness, and adjust your methods accordingly; and do not deviate from the proper course for those who study this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	for the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or turn; then apply a small piece of cotton soaked in egg white or persillie juice on the eye; afterwards heat the cautery which is shaped like this: it should be attached to the head like the shape of a feather from an owl, but if you wish, it can go from one side of the head to the other, and if you prefer, it can resemble a tent; however, in any case, the part that is attached will need to be moved for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, then work on it, and draw out the contents; afterwards apply a hot cautery, and hold your hand to the cautery above the eye, so that your hand does not do foolishly; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you proceed to the beginning of the cautery until the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then begin the cautery again once more, and do it another time if you need to, and leave it for three days; afterwards apply cotton soaked in butter, and treat with a desiccative ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and proceed according to what would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for fistulas which some of the ancients described.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Attend to the fistula and cut it open; afterwards place in the incision some finely powdered substance of which this is the formula:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it in the quantity of one .3. of lead; and hold your hand on the powder firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into their eye; and it is necessary to place over the patient's eye a cotton ball moistened with egg white or water: the lead thus seals the fistula, and heals wonderfully.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have described, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer a puncture with a knife, and to bring the fistula back into the body of the knife according to what is proper in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Cracks in the lips, which are called "hairs," often occur, especially in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly in those cracks until it reaches the bottom; after that, treat the area with plaster until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the neck
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the neck or in the uvula, or at the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it becomes putrid and rotten and ages, becoming a fistula; then you cure it as we have said in divisions, but if that does not help: then it is necessary to apply the cautery according to the size of the fistula; after making an opening or hole in the fistula, hold your hand until the hot iron reaches deep inside and at the back; do this once or twice, then cure as we have said for treatments, until he is healed; if cured thus, it is good; if not, you must uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and treating it with medicine does not help, then place the head of the patient in your lap; after that, heat the cautery according to the following manner: place a chain on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside it quickly, and hold it so long that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cautery as you wish; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let them gargle for an hour and rinse out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the tooth that was moving becomes fixed, and the softened gum is restrained, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold, where there is actual cold, and the remedies of medicine do not help, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways: one by butter and one by fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery by butter is such that you take sheep's grease, and put it in a spoon of iron or brass; after this, take cotton and wrap around the tip of a tent, and dip it in melted butter, then quickly place it on the painful tooth and hold it until it cools down; and do this often until its effect reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it over the painful tooth, and apply a hot iron until the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cauteries together are such that you take an iron or bronze rod, and let it be thick so the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, from which the form will come after, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter during the urgency of this cautery, and then vigorously rub it; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And apply the cautery to whichever part you wish, according to your ability; and this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofulas are full of cold phlegm and do not respond to digestion through medicines, then heat the cautery as described below, and make two openings for the smoke to escape on the side opposite the cautery; place the hot cautery over the abscess once or twice if necessary until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to its size, and leave it in place for three days; then put moist wool soaked in butter until the burn is gone; afterward treat the area with ointments and plasters until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture overcomes the channels of the phlegm, and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first cleared by solutive medicines; after this, perform cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to reach the throat itself, but burn only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After this, perform another cautery at the joint of the neck to the base of the spine, and let the cauterizations called "clavile" be as we have described their form before; treat the area as we have previously instructed until it is healed.
de la toust	for cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the diseases of phlegm are cold and moist, and the patient does not have fever or dryness, and the illness is old, if you perform one cautery on the pectoral muscles in their places; and another cautery between the breasts above the pit of the stomach; let the cauterizations called "clavile" be according to the form described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you wish, perform cautery by pricking the entire area which is called "points" of which the form is described above in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or inquire around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the area as described previously, let the cauterizations be three lines according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cauterizations are lighter, make three of them at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After the patient is laid on his back and side; then lift the shoulder that is within the armpit with both of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two grooves as shown here:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the shoulder until it pierces to the side, and there would be four cautery marks in total; and for that one is made with a cautery which has three grooves, so the shape of the cauteries are six marks; and the nerves are as fine as a thread, and this is the shape of the cautery which has three grooves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is placed on this one nerve, which results in eight cautery marks.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After place the cautery pellets ground with salt; after make rest the patient, and let not move the limb for long time until it be well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which thing happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery navel, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come coldness and much moisture until it strains its constitution, and are multiplied the catarrh to him, and by usual methods of cure it profits not, then it is necessary that the patient be suspended on his back, and stretch out his legs and his arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From those afterwards I make three cauterizations. One with the spoon of pitch in the amount of two doses, for the entire cautery navel, and two cauterizations outside each side until the shape of the cauterizations forms at three angles, and there is such space between one and the other that they do not join together when they discharge pus; and let the cauterizations be so deep that they penetrate both sides of the body, and let the shape of the cauterizations be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cauterization in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and for those who fear this cauterization, cauterize by pricking and cutting one point on the stomach as much as you want; then cauterize throughout the entire cautery which is called "points.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the treatment that we had before, until he is well.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver suffers pain from cold and moisture and great flatulence, so that it is weakened from its natural temperament due to excesses; and if the patient is treated according to what we have said in divisions, and it does not help him, then the patient should be positioned on his right side; and apply three cauterizations according to this form and figure and size above the liver, beyond the hypochondria, where a man's ribs come together; and leave between each cautery the thickness of a finger; and let them be long in line with the body, and do not press too much on the whole cautery; and burn only up to half the heart, and let the patient stand upright on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is to cauterize these cauteries of the elbow, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the flesh, for you would dry up the entire body; and let it not reach the eye, for the flesh is very delicate there, and you know this well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too strongly; and if it is in the membrane, the pain is intense.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment is to be applied to the breasts, the patient must lie on their back with their head raised; then incise the area where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterizing iron which resembles a reed, as described in the form.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize until the wound is burned and reaches syphac, until all the pus is out; afterwards treat according to the treatment of boils until it is healed; and it does not suit anyone other than those who have studied extensively in the art of medicine, and whose hands these diseases have corrupted at some point.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may boldly proceed with the treatment, although it seems to me that caution is better.
dou cautere de pleuresin	for the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should use cauteries made from the roots of aristolochia for pleurisy in this manner: take a root of aristolochia as long as possible, and it should be as thick and long as your thumb; soften it in oil, and apply it to the fire, then cauterize once between the rib and the neck, and two small cauterizations slightly downward below the beard area; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclined towards the back a little; one cauterization in the armpit, another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, with two more on either side of the shoulder blade behind the one between the two shoulders; do not press hard but rather gently as if sniffing.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient ones said that certain men use a cautery of fire similar to the razor, and they heat it and place it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess; and thus the pain subsides, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear that the patient dies immediately, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it is ineffective, then they offer three methods of cautery that are all good.
