Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "cure contuse", and you make the patient who has this disease shave his hair on the forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead equally according to its length; and let one of the cuts be as two fingers wide in the middle of the forehead going down towards the nose, and the other two by each temple above the eyebrows, and beware of cutting into the arteries that are at both temples above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the width of three fingers across; then prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth to dry the blood, and place the spatumile sharp on both sides as shown in this form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape off all the flesh that is between the two cuts to the surface of the skin which is on top of the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second incision, and then pull out this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first groove the instrument called "cultellaire," and it is very well sharpened on one side, and on the other side it is smooth, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh of the chest, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle groove.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches the one near the chest, and then make another incision in the middle groove until the other side; and then draw out blood evenly, and press the area for blood collection; then place a piece of old cotton in each groove, and put on damp cloths made of wine, oil, and honey, and guard against abscesses; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and administer plenty of hot water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When cataracts come frequently to someone, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and the sight weakening, and the whites burned; and the hair falls out, and in the head there is a cold pain, and the patient sneezes; then you know by these symptoms that those matters and that catarrh do not come from but many veins, and if there is any remedy to be used, this is it.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient behind their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another on each side of the pit.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton there, and cover it with linen strips; then bind over with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and be careful of hot abscesses; when they are removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with things that excite growth, which cause flesh to rise.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and apply it to these wounds to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the obstruction of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Whatever falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, or stones from mines or similar things such as iron; seeds, such as lentils, beans, peas; or flowing substances such as water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other substance that does not fit into the ear and does not grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, then let a few drops of violet oil or sesamum oil be administered for extraction; and make them sneeze with something irritating, and plug their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and extend the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often force comes from this treatment; and if it does not come by force, then administer the extraction with fine tweezers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by the tweezers, that is good; if not, then administer extraction with a fine needle of thin double thread; and if it does not come out by this, make a silk thread and insert the tip of the thread into the ear canal tightly, and plug around the thread with soft wax so that no air can enter with the thread; then pull firmly outward, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take some bird glue and place on a small instrument suitable for this purpose, wrap a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull outward.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot avoid all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear as for an abscess to come down and spasm; and the manner of cutting is that you make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to her strength, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and cut a small opening at the root of the ear in the fat or hanging part; and let the cut be as crescent-shaped, until you reach the stone, then take it out with all your might, and suck quickly into your mouth; and treat her until she is well.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if this grain is inside and it swells, then proceed with its extraction; and if it cannot come out, then apply the following subtle spatumile according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And administer an incision of that swelling.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the swelling is moist due to moisture from the ear, until you have made many incisions; then extract it with fine forceps and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of water that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to sneeze forcefully first, and then stuff the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same side where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it comes out because of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your thumb and light ones, and heat them slightly on the fire; then put one stone in the patient's ear, and let it out from under his foot on the other side, and strike another stone over the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone upon stone until all the fluid comes out, and thus it will come out completely; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end of the reed into the patient's ear, and burn the other head with fire until the softer part of the reed is burned; then do the same with other reeds until all the fluid comes out, as we have said about the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the creature, if it is small like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, extract it with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in treating distillations, and if the treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that you examine the ear in sunlight: if any worms are visible, remove them with fine forceps, and if none are seen, use this formula:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finer end into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then gradually form it throughout the entire formula; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, plug around the formula with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective against worms, which you will find in the treatment of distillations; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, whose form is as follows as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let there be a narrow sieve of silver or brass above the small holes, and over it cover with cloth for dripping; and to press inside the distillation use an instrument of brass well made for this purpose, and if you wish take a razor and wrap around the tip carefully cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you want of your medicines in the tube, and let the tube be in the ear; then stuff thoroughly within the razor all the cotton, and press with your hand gently until the oil is distilled to the bottom of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little warmed by fire as you distill into the ear; and beware that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffiness of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with a hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to stuffiness from a wound, or foreign matter inside the ear, and sometimes this stuffiness comes completely within the ear, so that one cannot see it; and at other times the pus comes out of the hole, and then one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes completely inside and cannot be seen is difficult to heal in many cases, and when it can be seen, you should put the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see pus present, then perform this spatulation as described in this form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind entirely so that it does not split the ear; if the growth is of flesh from the body of the ear, hold it with fine forceps, and cut lightly until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the growth is deep in the ear, take a fine razor and warm it slightly over fire, then apply it to the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the growth where the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce it lightly, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a dressing in the ear according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this on some day until the wound is healed, or take a tent (surgical dressing) and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top; and if you see an inflamed ear, then you must draw out the tent and move another tent moistened in cerate made of rosin oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, then dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding which are used to treat hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papermakers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althethium that comes from the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch with pliers and forceps, and cut a piece from its root with a scalpel; then apply ground vitriol to the site.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if any remains unremoved, cauterize it with a fine lentil cautery and then incise to remove the remnants; and often they need repair because some part of their roots remain; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	from the hailSTONE (or depending on context, if referring
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, things that resemble hail in form and hardness come from the eyes, and for this reason, this disease is called "hail in the eye"; it is a collection of thick moisture in the membrane. The procedure is as follows: observe if the hail moves from side to side, which is easy to know; then cut around it widely, then gently peel each part, then take it out with forceps, and cut it away.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the skin slightly, do not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, sew it up with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not apply force, for the ointment will heal it quickly and regenerate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grain is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the skin and extract the grain with tweezers, and cut and press from both sides; and if the skin is moved by incision, it does not harm; and when the grain is removed, lift out the wound with salt water, and treat the area with a flesh-regenerating agent until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is generated in the membranes above the eyes, and this happens more often with children than with some people, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces immediately, and sleep like that, and their membranes below their eyebrows are moistened by the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press that place with your two fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient puts their head on your lap; and then take a piece of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity it contains of exinach from each part, then place it over them; and press with both hands from one side and the other so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then cut an incision through the moisture with a sharp spatula, no wider than the opening made for phlebotomy; and cut the skin properly until you reach the exinach; and in many cases, the exinach comes out from the incision, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull it out then in one piece of torn cloth when you remove it, and move your hand right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to insert anything into the wound, do not bring all the spatumile up to the eye, do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrement does not appear at the beginning of the wound, gently enlarge the wound slightly until it appears; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, place them on the site, and extract bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to a hot place, then treat it with plasters that alleviate until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the eyelashes
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in the eyes other than those naturally there and they irritate them, they cause various ailments such as habitual tears and inflammation of the eyelids and conjunctiva, to the point that it leads to the destruction of the eyes; and the cure follows four methods: either by cautery with fire together, or by medicine according to what is mentioned in the chapter on cautery before this one, and is done through incision and suturing, or by cauterization, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand; if it turns over, that is good; if not, insert a needle along the entire lid margin where the hairs grow among these hairs, and stretch the lid upwards to the razor; then cut into the part below the eyelid, below the inserted hairs, reaching from the main tear duct to the auxiliary one; then remove the thread, and place beneath the eyelid a small pad of cotton and gauze, then sew onto the eyelid a figure resembling the leaf of myrtle, and regardless, it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you wish to elevate the eyelid which is planned for.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs that the paper be cut in great quantity according to how the paper is softened; then make on all the spatula along the II lines which you have marked, and start from the large tear up to small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the needle in one of the II angles of the kerchief, then peel it off entirely; then sew together the II lips with a stitch of one thread of fine linen, and wipe away the blood, and arrange the superfluity of the threads over the II eyebrows with some sticky things if you wish to do this; and if not, take no care for it, then leave the suture and the threads up to III days or IV; then cure the wound without a suture made of drying and binding materials, because the paper rises immediately at the moment of the wound and its assembly, but the suture is cumbersome (as the ancients say), and this work is without fear; and there is another way: which is that you mark the paper with a shape that is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, to III needles apart according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those which rise above the small areas evenly according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the things are not even, then take a needle with a thread, and place it in the figure; and attach another thread near the large artery, and the second thread near the small one, and join between your two threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have described, then join the two edges of the wound by suturing, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; but sometimes the hair on the paper is turned: in such cases, use what we have said about the incision; however, the suture in both cases requires more skill.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the canthi is according to this form: and it is that you turn the paper and cut into it as I have said, and then make two canthi by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatumile are; and attach them to the two corners where you hold the threads; then join one and the other finely on what protrudes from the paper of the eye, and pull the two canthi from both sides firmly; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is pulled will die off and heal and grow back, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and if the paper is raised, and no hair will grow there anymore; and this is the form of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle and put a thin silk thread through it; then join the ends of the hair and tie them together finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread in the comb briefly, and knot the ends of the thread; then have the patient place their head on your hand; and let this be done near the sun so that the work is clear, for it is a subtle and delicate task, then insert the needle through the hair root adjacent to it quickly as you pull it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the comb, and put into the comb those hairs if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the hairs become visible throughout the comb with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is treated and does not come out with it, pull the hair to the root along with all the thread you have attached to it until the hair comes out from its follicle and you can see it by sight; then pull out the hair and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows up; and if the hair is short, attach one long hair to the natural hairs, and lift it with the one you left behind, until it is pulled out.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pus of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or pus comes to the eye, there are two ways it can occur: one naturally, and the other unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly by a wound, or from cutting, or from cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment is that you should split open the closure, separate its edges, and place linen tents inside, keeping it apart until it heals; and it is not appropriate to use in its treatment things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but use things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and prepare a lotion with water or ale and flax seeds boiled, and apply ointment made from melted wax mixed with some oil, and wrap a bandage around it, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you guard against it not healing according to the form it was before; and these works which we have said are nothing other than remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth, and it is natural causes and accidents.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the method of treatment is that you take a needle, with which there are two threads, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out in two places on the flesh; then stretch the flesh over all the needle, and cover it with a patch about one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is needed, it is good; if not, take the scraper and place it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side within the paper; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two corners of the incision that you have made, and make them form a single angle so that when they are joined together, the figure is as if the letter has the name «I griesche»; then remove that flesh according to the acuteness of its sides beneath the paper, from what lies under the paper, then join the two separated parts with thread; then apply the treatment of what we have said concerning softening medicines and tents until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a fissure or seam or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full cut beneath the hairs of the paper skin, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent as I have said; and one should perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters prepare ingeniously with all their power how to return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what requires work and instruments in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden swelling of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in such a manner that the skin above is swollen with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should insert the tip of a razor under the skin, and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, until you cut away what adheres to the delicate spatumile, which must not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot bear a razor that is too sharp and does not irritate the eye; and your incision, by which you peel off this assembly, should be lightly made, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and heal completely this assembly, and sometimes put salt water in the eye, and lift it with fresh water; then place between the skin and the eye a linen patch, and apply moistened wool over an abundance of egg white; and after three days use poultices and soothing remedies until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: one is nervous and similar to hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but is like frozen white moisture, so when one touches it with iron and thinks to remove it with pincers, it cannot be done; and both kinds begin near the large tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all of the vision and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the incision is that the patient places their head on your lap, then you work the eyes; and lift the membrane with your hand, then coil the nail with pincers gently, and lay it above; then take a needle, and put horsehair, or deer hair, or ox hair, and strong thread; and double the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, and pierce through completely with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and lay it above, and cut along all the hair on the side of the nail that covers the pimple and the silk to the top, then trim the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with the fine spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct so that by the incision tears do not come out habitually; and sometimes lay the nail only on the little finger, and on the thread as we have said; then cut along all the underlying membrane according to this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the sutures do not touch the tender flesh and break it, and that the stitches are not pierced; and after the incision, pour a little ground pitch into the eye, and make an application from litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not loose and you cannot insert a needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this kind of nail condition is often treated with various medicines; it grows as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, proceed carefully with the patient's eye, and take the suture gently according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently from above, and if you see that it is thinning and the tissue around it is tight, then drip from your mouth into the eye an application made of litharge and red litharge and ground pitch, and plug the eye until the next day; then continue with the work according to this same method until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then treat it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid harms the eye by great injury, then suspend it at the nail, and cut a part but not all so that no tears come forth; then drop into the eye red chyle which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some people's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, restraining it from moving and turning it outward, resembling a blue anemone; and the treatment is that the patient places his head on something firm, then works on the eye, and coils all that flesh with appropriate hooks, supporting it firmly; then cut the first layer of flesh and proceed to scrape until completion, taking care not to injure the eye during work; make the incision according to what we have described in cutting nails and for removing small particles, as illustrated later in this chapter; when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, apply the eye with ground seed or drop red chyle and similar corrosive medicines, then place cotton outwardly coated with egg white to ensure it does not develop a hot abscess; if anything remains and a hot boil appears, fearing an abscess, treat it with things that soothe a hot abscess; return to your work until it is healed, and thus proceed when such flesh adheres in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you treat each weak eye by the natural way; and by the accidental way, with iron work; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member can bear that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that cover the eye are visible in their work and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first you must check if the eye, in which the disease is present, is healthy except for this disease; then treat it in such a manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your hand, then suspend those veins along the whole eyelid according to your wisdom, and let the eyelids be delicate double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two needles be placed at intervals on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, when you coil the veins gently with forceps, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins coming out of the eye; and be careful not to strike the eye with the points of the forceps, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so as not to miss any of the veins; and when you have done this, then drop into the eye a green and red collyrium to dissolve what remains of the sore.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect all of it at that hour, then apply a poultice to the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and is assured of a warm abscess, then restart according to this manner as described above until he is healed; and this is the form of the procedure:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physician calls this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it does not heal, there is pus that you must cut open where it needs to be lanced, and drain all the moisture that is inside until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, remove it with all the instruments as described here; it is called "aspre chief," and should be made of iron bent into a head like a file, as shown in the current form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands and press gently until you know that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the area with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the tissue is adhered and flesh grows there, and the body of the bowel is adhered, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew itself and is not inflamed, no bad accident happens, then know that he is well; if not, you must return the fistula to the anus according to this form: and open the bone a second time with an instrument, and by using dry medicines, and when it is opened take one probe according to this form, and make the head of iron at three angles, and the shaft should be slender up to the point as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the lamina, and move your hand from the eye one finger's width, then rotate the entire probe until it pierces the bone and the patient feels wind if they hold their hand over their anus; then restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and toughens the tissue, let the matter go to the anus; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is completely open and there is no disturbance or reduction in vision, you must bind the patient; then cleanse it, then apply suction cups without striking to draw out impurities, then place on the eye a plaster made of cedar, aloes, incense, and myrrh, and then press the eye; and cover with bandages and cloths; the method for the cloths is that you should take soft cloths and double each one four times, and then place them one over another according to the size needed by the eye; then press it firmly under a hard bandage; and again apply suction cups without striking; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the plaster becomes loose, you must tighten it much; then remove the dressing after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, restart the application of plasters, cloths, bandages, and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the tearing of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then it is opened up, and forceful paper strips are applied like resin grains, and it is frightening to see; then if you wish to repair it, work as if you were inserting a needle into the root of the part below until you reach the one above, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the eyebrow part; make holes and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut the area with double threads and tie one part of the cloth tightly around it, squeeze out the needle and put on wet wool soaked in plenty of egg whites; let it be until the thread falls off with the cloth, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; sometimes the wound is restrained by a circular bandage of cloth from each side until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears swollen, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes in line with the eye, and draw out the cloudy moisture and let the eye descend; then extract until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a swelling in the eye that resembles an aqueous discharge, though it is not actually an aqueous condition; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on a properly arranged and straight chair, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the swelling come to the top towards your eyes; then if it remains there without descending and obscuring the light, know that it is an aqueous condition, and if the descent of the swelling does not appear as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Seat the patient between your hands, then take the spatula and cut through the corneous membrane at one point along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneous membrane and the corona, until the bow comes out; and when it has come out, drip in hot honey mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat it further until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing them; act according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and hold the healthy eye firmly; then place the paper of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye; then take with your right hand, if it is the left eye, the instrument called "almagda," or with your left hand if it is the right eye; then place the tip of the instrument next to the corona by a thickness of one hair on that clear part of the eye near the lower tear duct, and then insert the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, turning your hand until it penetrates the clear part of the eye, and feel when the almagda reaches an empty space; and it should be that the length of the path of the almagda is perfectly equal to the distance from the pupil to the end of the dark area; this is the corona of the eye; you will see the bone on the paper through the clarity of the corneous membrane, and then place the instrument where the water is, then press it out one path at a time.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water flows now, let the patient see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, if the water rises again through the second passage, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly placed and it does not rise, gently extract almagda by turning your hand little by little; then add a bit of powdered gemstone to the water, and lift the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place outside the eye plugs made of linen soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg white, and bind it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply it mixed with plenty of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people who have eyes that are too hard, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then insert the almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a dormitory in which they sleep on their back in a dark place; and be careful of all movements, and give them light foods, and do not move their head to right or left, and bind them according to their disposition until the third day; then unbind them in that same dark room, and test their vision, showing them some things, and then rebind them until the seventh day; and it is not necessary to do this during the hour of treatment or immediately after incision, but you must wait because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses form, that you should unbind the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to him who treats abscesses; and when it is alleviated, then loosen the sight and place on its face a patch for several days, and let it be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and resume his duties; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they perform almagda piercings, to which one attaches water, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almonds, for those who do not recognize them; and they are properly of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh growths on the nose appear in various forms, some of which resemble many-legged scorpions; and there are such cases where the flesh is swollen with red coloring, and there is healthy flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of this flesh that is healthy and not swollen, you should seat the patient between your hands facing the sun; work his nostrils, and apply a lancet to those growths, and draw out the pus; then proceed as much as you can sustain with a fine sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all of the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any substance that cannot be cut, treat it with the finest instrument gently, so nothing remains; and if pus overflows from the abscess, carefully clean it as is appropriate; and if these are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the pus is dried up and all the flesh is removed, then apply fresh water or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If urine flows and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not flow as it should, know there is flesh grown on the bone above, which the instrument cannot cut: then you must put a thick linen thread in it, and tie knots with your hands, leaving at least one space between each knot; and place the patient's finger in his mouth to pull out through the nose until it comes out of the mouth; and many times children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for those who wish to do it; then hold one end that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and pull one after the other carefully as you untie the knots.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the new tissue has corrupted the old flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then place a silver chain in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, where one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And whether it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a chain, and the conduit should be similar; and if you wish, make a closed chain, and let the instruments be full for purging the head; and have I handle at the top to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" is born on the head of the nose, and it grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye; and for this reason, you must cut it at the beginning, remove all flesh from it, then place the cautery or burning medicine upon it. And if one delays in cutting it when it is large, beware if it is hard, of a bad color, and lacks sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an embedded abscess, for when you cut it even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to touch, not of a bad color, and you see that all can be removed, then empty the patient's body and cut it without fear, and treat the area with dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilage works, there is little benefit, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
