Then when this happens to anyone, look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips in one seam, and treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are torn apart on both sides, you must scrape all parts of their edges until they bleed, then bring together the two lips in one seam, bind it, and put powder on, powdered dragon's blood and ground incense; and apply a piece of hot or other adhesive plaster over the powders, and leave it until it peels off by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the abdomen; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In some people, hard abscesses appear on the lips, resembling grains of wheat, both small and large; then you must turn the lips, cut into each node, grasp it with forceps, and remove it in each part; then fill the area after making an incision using broiled vitriol until the blood is congealed; and then clean the wound with a dressing, and treat the area with dry remedies until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often a piece of flesh grows on the gums that the ancients called "albulus"; you must hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, allowing the pus or blood to flow; then apply vitriol powder ground up, or other powders that are constricting and drying; if this flesh returns after cutting, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: it will not return after cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of dirtiness/discharge
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are assembled in the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, crusts that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, or green, to such an extent that corruption reaches the gum, and the tooth becomes foul-smelling; you must have the patient sit between your hands, place their head in your lap, and remove the teeth or crusts thoroughly until nothing remains; do this for the blackness and greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are clean; if you extract what is there at first, that is good; if not, start again on the second day and third, until everything has been removed; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work reveals, because the tools used to extract teeth from their sockets have different shapes than those used between the teeth; these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth from its pain that you delay drawing it out as much as you can, for no one should do this; for it is a very high substance until there be no excuse for pulling it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to draw it out, you must be certain of the tooth that needs to be pulled.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain deceives the patient, and they believe it is from a healthy tooth, pulling out a good tooth; yet the pain does not depart by this means until the bad one is extracted, as we have seen many times with these patients. And when you are certain of the painful tooth, you should thoroughly char around the tooth for about two phalanges strongly to protect the gum from all sides; then pull it out gently using your fingers or fine forceps little by little until it comes loose, then firmly secure the forceps; and hold the patient's head between your knees so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth directly without breaking it, and if it does not come out forcefully, take any of these instruments and push on each side gently, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and decayed, you must fill it with strips of cloth where the hole is; and carefully pull it out with pliers so that it does not break when pulling; and you must very skillfully work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and return to the patient due to the mischief of the root greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not act as ignorant surgeons do, who because of their haste and boldness sometimes break the tissue, and do not properly treat what we have described; but instead they often cause great illness by touching the roots or tissues that remain, as we have frequently seen; and when the tooth is removed, wash the area with wine or hyssop and salt; and if bleeding continues, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not double when you extract the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick parts so that they do not bend when extracting, and they should be made of well-forged iron, and should be toothed to hold the grip.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, it is necessary to place cotton moistened with butter on the site for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is softened, then you can insert pincers called "algefri," which resemble a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out completely with these forceps, you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the instrument called "althali," which is in fact a plane, here is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps from this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two prongs, here is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments which are mentioned before in the reason of teeth, and of this instrument which seems like large forceps, here is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be such that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of bone exist; and also other instruments which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their work and the illness shows them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of cases; if one breaks the cartilage or other bones, it may rot, so seek among the instruments that I have told you about, and help with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, remove it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth does not appear according to its natural position in the body, and the form is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you must know if the tooth has grown after the other teeth, and it is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down: then cut it; and if it grows crooked with respect to the other teeth, take this instrument whose shape is here described, and resembles a small beak, and let it be made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it a little at a time over several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and so as not to move the others, and if it appears that you can file it, then file it with a tool like this one whose shape is shown:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth little by little over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks off; then smooth it at the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then you must file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth lock
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth become locked together, whether due to impact or falling, and the patient cannot press down on what they are eating without it causing them to defecate, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but this has not helped; then you must restrain them with a gold thread, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never moves; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and place it double between two healthy teeth, then put the knot between any one or more loose teeth until you carefully reach a healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering until you return to where you started, and pull your hand subtly and carefully so that nothing moves; and let your tying be at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the teeth of the wire with pliers, and join them together, and place it between the healthy tooth so that it does not injure the tongue; and then leave it as tight as possible for as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the wire falls out, tighten it again with another wire; thus it will endure and serve in this way throughout its life, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and of the two defective ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, replace it in its place, fresh with fresh, as we have said; and do not interfere with anyone who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes one makes a form of a tooth from bone of a fish, and places it where the defect is, and tightens it as we have said, and it will endure and serve for such a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the bandage of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is this bandage that comes from under the tongue either by nature at birth; or due to an accidental wound that has healed; and the procedure is such that you work on the mouth of the patient with their head in your lap, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous bandage widely until the tongue is free from its attachment, and if there is hardness or a knot, which is from the sudden healing of a wound, then insert a hook and cut it open widely; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery lies beneath; and when you have done this, wash the area with rose water and cold water, then place under the tongue a dressing of linen; and each night change the bandage so that the wound does not heal over.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place over the area ground vitriol; and if it weakens the blood, cauterize with a gentle cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it colored black or hard and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a carbuncle; and if it inclines towards blanching and there is moisture, pour in liquid silver and cut it with a fine scalpel, and release it from both sides; and if your work weakens the blood, place ground vitriol until it congeals, then return to your work until you have treated all aspects; then lift the area gently and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	At times, lumps come into the throat which are called "godath," and they are properly known as the two tonsils; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healthy, be careful: if these abscesses are hard, slightly sensitive, and of a dusky color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is swollen, do not touch them with iron, nor for bloodletting; but leave them until they turn black, and then you will remove them, as they would naturally break off; and if they are of a pale color and the root is delicate, prepare the instrument to cut, but first check whether the abscess lies at rest and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head in your right hand, and open his mouth and grasp the tongue with both hands below with all the instrument, which is of this form; it should be made of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	As you press the tongue with all this instrument and see an abscess, take a lancet and insert it into the almond, and draw it out forcefully above as far as you can; then pull some material from the tissues with it, then cut around the area with the instrument, which is of this form, resembling forceps; and nonetheless, the ends are curved, one opposite the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, cut it with pincers, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be cutting on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the glands, cut the other in the same manner, then after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and warm and soothing liquids, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with hot water or cooked pomegranate rind, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stilled; then treat him until he is healthy; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two glands, so cut them as you would the two glands equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed in her throat, specifically the tonsillitis; and I found it almost completely obstructing her throat so that she could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she remained like this one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had two fingers' width through both openings of the anus.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then and inserted an arrowhead into one, pulled it out forcefully, and removed a large portion of pus; then I did the same on the other opening of the anus, and operated on her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the arrowhead into the abscesses, and some part came out, but only a little blood; thus, the throat passage of the woman was cleared, and she now began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting this abscess for a long time; the abscess kept growing quickly, filling up the place that I had emptied until it became very large again; then I treated it and cauterized inside her throat: thus, it stopped growing; and I left these parts, and do not know what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye睑藏详情可见之处似乎没有
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the eye and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is detached, large, and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the diffuse abscesses are alleviated, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is round and assembled and is not elongated; and it is bloody or of dusky color or black, then you must avoid cutting.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, based on its blueness and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we made mention earlier; then insert the lancet into the uvula, and draw it down, and cut at point I of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two tonsils.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut beyond the excess that lies outside the natural boundary; for if you cut more, you will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said regarding the incision of the two tonsils, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary that you use an instrument for the cautery to calm their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of the cautery is sharp and acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient place their head on your lap, and then press the tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and cover it with sharp vinegar, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and apply this instrument to the affected area, here is the form of which:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on the head a container where the medicine is applied, as much as would fit in a spoon, and apply the instrument to all the medicine over the eye; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine without it going down their throat; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour until you see it darken and the medicine's irritation subsides; if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with the cotton on top of the eyelid, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry for four or five days. If you need to restart the application of the medicine, then start again after the cautery, wipe around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what remains of the medicine; then rinse with cold water and gargle as needed until they are well.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation according to this method, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and gather them all together or any of them in one pot, and add salt, and boil it; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have an instrument pointed according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or brass, and place one end of the instrument in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the affected area through the vein, until the area is necrotized; after this, repeat often, until the area dries up, and beware that you do not perform this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things happen then; and do not perform it unless the abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a chain and put an eggshell inside the head of the sick person so that their mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or thorn from fish gets stuck in the throat or something else; you must then extract what you can see, and press the tongue with sunlight across all the instruments so that you may detect the object; and for what you cannot discern and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit as if the food were cooked in their stomach; perhaps this will expel the foreign object by vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or seaweed, or lettuce root, or dry bread; attach a thread to the sponge and then guide it down; when it reaches the site, it will catch hold, and then pull out with force; if these methods do not work as mentioned above, take an instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest breathing be obstructed, nor push in the bone; and move it so that the patient puts in the instrument, so that it moves where the thing is loose; if you push down, or pull out completely, equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood is treated, as I said in the division, by curing it with medicines; and when this does not help, then examine the patient's throat in the sunlight, pressing their tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook or fine forceps.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hooked cane and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert a hot iron into the hook of the cane, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is covered in water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full jar of cold water and pour it into the mouth, and have them swallow it down; and move their hand frequently; as soon as the blood feels the water, it will flow.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not flow as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida using the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of grapes; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot with live coals, and cover it with a perforated lid, through which passes the tube of the instrument; then you throw in your fumigation, and have the patient place his chin on the tube, and close the mouth, so that no smoke escapes but goes up to the blood; and now the blood will flow, and if it does not flow, repeat the fumigation several times; and allow the patient thirst, and eat salty and sour things, and do not drink water; then it will be necessary for it to come out forcefully by this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood, when it can be seen, resembles curved tongs for entering into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and there are rough edges like a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what the memory brings forth later in this and that chapter, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is similar to its own type, and from those it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses of the flesh area are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one must not pierce until the swelling is complete according to its fulfillment; and there are such as need to be pierced when they are hard, and do not die off according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it is fully rotten, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near a principal limb, and you delay puncturing it until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; when it is near the fundament, puncture it as soon as it becomes dead; and it does not behoove to pierce an unripe abscess before complete digestion, except for one that is near the fundament, so that it does not rot completely, become elongated inside, and a fistula develops; and cannot heal in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of puncturing an abscess that has become dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the fever subsides, and there is a decrease in pain and redness, and hardening and sharpness at the top of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform puncturing where the abscess depends most, and where it appears pus; and let the puncture be along the body, and if the abscesses are on hands or feet, in joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equally where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases of bleeding, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, it is better to wait until it is confirmed to be in complete resolution before proceeding with puncture, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before then, the body of its venom will be elongated, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance the lips and depth of it may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that needs to be punctured according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small punctures; and large abscesses with large punctures, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where it is necessary to cut deeply, and to excise; when they have become as hard as leather and are swollen, you should treat them as you would boils: and there are some that are divided into three angles, and there are others that are excised like a myrtle leaf, as with shoulder abscesses; and there are those where a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar excisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce thoroughly; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that time, but draw out part of it; then plug up the abscess until the next day, then draw some more out again; do this little by little over many times, until all the pus comes out; similarly if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or young children, or old men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the breath sometimes stops when the pus comes out, which might cause the patient to die, and you would not be at fault.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and check if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a wide opening, use pieces of linen or old cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and there are many openings, place a piece in each so that they come together against one another; and if you have cut into the skin around the abscess and sewn it closed, fill it with dry cotton or flax shavings without moisture, and leave it bandaged until the third day; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, administer cold and soothing water, and wet the cloth, placing it repeatedly on the bleeding area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, administer regulation and treatment, and use the powders I have mentioned earlier in this book. If it is winter and the area where the abscess is located is very nervous, you must place tents and cloths soaked in wine and warm oil; and if it is summer and the area is fleshy, you should place cloths soaked in water and oil or cold wine and oil until the third day as we have said. Then open the abscess, clean it, and treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this one must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of sweats
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	For small abscesses in the head come in various forms, like the spots on a gooseberry, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and contain moisture like pus; and there are others that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work on the waist is such that you must test all the instruments called "entromissoire," of which the forms come next, and what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if there is moisture, then cut it above the long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied out, then scrape without leaving any part of the skin that contained the moisture, for it returns quickly if anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply to the wound, and leave until the next day; and those who remain from the night will heal.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart with the cotton as before on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds onto fat, cut it according to this form, longitudinally; and throw out all your ounces, and skin it from all sides, and put all your effort into draining the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for an abscess if it contains stones, cutting and scraping as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when you incise an abscess containing stones and it is moist, it is easier to treat, as there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses are in the head where there is no moisture, and among them were the abscesses that I incised on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had struck any part of it, it would have caused a wound like striking a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, whether those that come to the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the incision should always be made as far down as possible, so that the pus may exit; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	These abscesses often occur in the neck, and sometimes they are seated elsewhere, and become inflamed, and at times they appear in other parts of the body, and are very painful, growing one upon another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own area, as the knot and the head abscess are, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one then that you see to be well disposed for touching, and it resembles the color of the skin, and is soft on all sides and is not hard against the neck veins or arteries or conduit, and is not deep; you must cut it from above, and peel off the skin from each part, and stretch the two lips of the wound with needles, if you need to, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and cut little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the pusumile not be sharp or cutting, so your hand does not slip, and do not go too far, lest you cut what should not be cut.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work on it, place in the wound vitriol ground into powder, or some powders that constrict blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and then begin to dress it.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is constricted, return to your work until you complete it; then search with your proper tool if there remain any small scrofulas, and cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not right that you should cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with double strong thread, and let it fall from there without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the whole scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, since there is no excess tissue due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	Then you must focus on cutting the root of it, pulling out the force, and sewing as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold excess tissue, pierce there where it appears to die; and pierce them as previously mentioned, depending on the situation, then administer treatments with ointments and similar things, so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, treat it with ointment healing flesh until it heals.
de squinance	of squeezing
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the incision of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squeezing, it is necessary to remove the fold in the throat which is called "epiglottis"; and one should not provide assistance by this means, because all the veins and the phlegm of the patient are affected by hot abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the phlegm, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger of choking.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we make a small incision across three circles or four, between two circles in the thickness of the mucous membrane, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for cutting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from end to end.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the neck to its full length, then cuts the windpipe until it reaches the tracheal rings; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the mucous membrane as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm in the part that has been broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed from which one fears strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew it all up without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the need arises.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he will breathe through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason, the ancient ones commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, which takes three or four days, and then they ordered it stitched up and cleaned until it was clean; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and found the blood that had come out, and I knew well that she had not cut a vein or main artery, but rather the wind was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until she was healed; and the only consequence for the lady was that her voice became hoarse, and afterwards she returned to her usual state; therefore I say that there is no need to fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of jet, and it occurs frequently in women; and it happens in two ways: naturally, and accidentally; a natural one does not have an abscess root.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one happens in two ways, of which one is similar to fatty tissue, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it does not befit to operate except on the small one, and examine and search throughout the interior: if you find it as fatty tissue, and cannot reach any vein, then cut it out like cutting fat, and remove all its covering, if there is any; and quickly investigate thoroughly, and treat it appropriately until it is completely healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	We have many ways, of which I will describe all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to tell all the differences that exist between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that when it is fever and heat holding on, until the boiling is past, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and the heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a swelling, which is its own sac and matches the color of the skin, and begins like a boil; and they vary in consistency, being either hard or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of the nose that you first examine and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire," according to their form which will appear in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining abscesses in the nose is that you take the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers back and forth, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the entromissoire, and be careful not to use excessive force.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture continues to flow out when cut, regardless of its color, proceed as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire no more moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then make a cross incision, take it with forceps, and lightly scrape from each side while taking care of the coat where it lies so you can remove it intact with the nose; and if you cannot remove it intact, cut it into pieces so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains within it, the pus will return many times; and if some remains a little bit, and the blood does not hurt, apply to the wound some corrosive powder, and hold open the wound, and place hot poultices on the abscess, and treat with other remedies until it is healed; and if the pus is great, sew together both lips of the wound, and heal by that which generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein resists or is contrary to you, hasten and apply the place with ground vitriol, and let it lie for two days or three, until the wound becomes putrid, and allow the boiling of the blood; then return to cleaning what remains of the pus.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of instruments for probing, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one that is called "breb," and they exist in three ways: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistulas; and they are also like the needles used to sew boils, and are made of brass or iron or silver, and those which are yellow are more valuable, and for encircling bends of fistulas, solid ones are better than hollow ones; and they exist in three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of lancets are very diverse, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are lancets that have two curves in three ways; and there are lancets that have three curves, and they are also in three ways; and there are lancets with two curves, and lancets with only one curve, and these are also in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tip of these instruments that are used for cutting is sharp, and there are some that cut only on one side to avoid cutting the veins or nerves; and among those introduced, the lancets are held in handles so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses; and they come in three types: large, small, and medium-sized, as you see; and these are used only in soft tissues such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas; and sometimes one makes another instrument smaller, resembling the bark of a fistula, according to this form, for which one stops blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed at the site that corresponds to the cutting of veins, and arteries, and sometimes follows this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the testicles of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, swelling so much that they seem like women's breasts; and remain deformed and swollen, and if one wishes to treat them, it must be done according to this form from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicine that heals flesh to the wound, then sew together the two edges of the wound, and treat it until it is healed; if the testicle descends downwards and becomes soft due to its size as happens with women, cut it into two halves above through two similar incisions, so that one end joins the other, such that the larger part contains the smaller according to this form from line b to the line g; then scrape off the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and proceed as we have said about suturing and powders, and whatever else is necessary for treatment until it heals; if it does not heal or the incision is not fully made because the patient refuses to rest or due to excessive bleeding, you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in a caustic ointment; leave it until it consumes the remaining parts and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are hard types of scrofula with edges, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to the line .g.:[\]
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus inside the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment as needed until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles a scrofula, cut it as we have said about cutting scrofulas, and if the wound contains pus, treat it with cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sealed, there are often abscesses that form; similarly, this happens with a swollen vein and an abscess. And when you recognize it as being from the artery, the abscesses are long and profound; and when you feel them with your fingers, they feel constricted; and when it is from the vein, it appears soft and diffuse; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially if it is under the armpits and in the angles and on the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
