ask them both if any part of the intestine is wrapped around the hard white fat, and if you find anything, remove it from underneath; then take a needle with one thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it in the back part of the fat layer, which is after the skin of the scrotum; after the waist, cut the ends of the threads so there are four threads left; then arrange them one over another like a cross, and tie up the fat layer, of which we have spoken as being under the skin of the scrotum, with a strong thread from two sides; then wrap the threads of the stitches together tightly on both sides, so that no foreign matter can enter and cause an abscess; put back the bandage according to the first long bandage twice its width; and after these two bandages leave uncovered one finger's width of the fat layer under the scrotum; and then cover all the rest following the roundness that the testicle forms; then cut in the part below the skin of the scrotum, as much as the groin and the bowels, as we have said before; then apply moistened flaxseed oil to the wounds, and place the bandages as we have described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white tissue that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the ligament fall by itself as it should; and if it delays in falling, soak it with hot water, and place what we have said on it until it falls naturally; then treat the wound with another method, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the condition where the intestines are involved, in such a way that you bind the vessels, above the navel lightly towards the back; then cut into them, and treat the abscess with what we have described, until the vessels release; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes there is a rupture in the groin area, as we have said, and it becomes apparent; and no part of the intestines descends into the scrotum, but if they do descend, it is an emergency requiring constant care; and yet if it remains too long at this point, the wound or rupture will worsen, causing the intestines to descend; and this happens due to the extension of the groin area as we have said, because it becomes extended, then softened and swollen, and apparent; and the treatment for this is by cautery, as we have previously mentioned; sometimes it is treated with a knife in this way: the patient lies supine on their back between your hands, then cut around the swollen part of the groin to an extent of three fingers' width; then extract the tissue below the skin that follows, and take the thread and place it over the apparent area of the groin tissue; press firmly against the belly, then sew both sides of the apparent areas of the groin tissue onto the head of the thread, and sew one to the other; then remove the head of the thread, and do not cut any more tissue or stretch the egg or anything else, as I have told you in treating the rupture of the intestines; finally treat it according to the method for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, mend and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The tissue is constricted, and there is no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is ineffective in this place, and closer to being harmful.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the genitals often becomes softened in some men because the tissues inside become softened and milk can be seen; and when one wishes to treat it, have the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin over the natural skin; then stitch together the two lips at one seam, and if you wish, sew the excess soft skin along three or four seams firmly; then cut between the seams, and treat it as other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is prohibited by our law, and for that reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; but it is necessary for two reasons: one is that the priest knows how to respond when asked about it, and knows how to perform the treatment; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform by traction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles become soft and hanging down; then hold them with your hand until they are retracted and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of animals: you should anesthetize the beast, and press the skin on its testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory bandage, and cut each testicle in one stroke when they have been well flayed; and leave some of the fatty tissue and the delicate fat that is over the vessels; and this method of castration is gentler than that which is done by traction, because with traction there may be left behind something from the testicles, which makes the beast desire lust; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Regarding hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is in two ways among men: one is that between the two testicles it has the appearance as the figure of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes encircles the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is for women, and tie it around the wrist like a rod with two cords.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for a man and a woman is that you cut away all adhering tissues, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine sprays on the skin of the genitals, there is no specific treatment.
de la tentigene	of the examination
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a tissue adhering to the genital area, making it very unpleasant to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is how it is treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the excess of the tentigene with your hand or scissors, and cut it lightly; do not go too deep, so that no blood comes out, then treat it like other wounds until it heals; and for another tissue that appears at the entrance of the vagina, remove it, and sometimes it may bleed, and it resembles a horn, and because of this, the ancients called it "horn disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary to treat it as we have said about tendinitis, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratic when the nature of a woman's body is not perceived, or when the passage is small; and it is by nature from birth, or due to illness that has occurred; or because of added flesh, or thin or thick tissue, and is formed perfectly in the womb, or on the sides, or inside; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps menstruation; and knowledge of this comes from examining the part.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If constipation is apparent nearby, I desire it to be treated with your two fingers or with the right [instrument].
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle syphilis and it is near the two books, hurry, and proceed thus: place your two fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two books firmly, until the subtle syphilis lies flat over the swelling; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and place it on the site, and let the woman rest lying face down each day, so that she cannot sit.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syphilis is hard and thick, then you should scrape it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh growth, suspend it and scrape it; and have medicines that staunch blood, such as hawthorn berries, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with a large amount of egg; then apply a poultice of flax wide enough so the wound cannot heal over; and in this manner treat it for a long time, and apply a dry bandage of linen; then continue treatment with other methods until he is well.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh is corrupted in a wound, it must be cut according to this manner, except for deeply seated abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the deeply seated abscess which is in the wound, one must not cut it open.
des emorroides	about hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are protrusions of veins that often occur without proper care, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn hard; we have already mentioned in the section the appearances of them, and the signs, and here I will say those which respond to treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and hard lumps, when they are perfectly formed in the wound and do not appear to the touch, cannot be cured by cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who have the mouth of the ulcer, which can be felt, are those who can be treated by cleaning.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Then you must place the woman in a cold house, then stretch the altar with tongs, and cut it off at its roots, then sprinkle medicine that restrains blood, such as oak bark and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gall nuts and similar things, and then take oatmeal, and boil it with honey and oil, and use it to make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have the patient undergo cupping on the back and breasts without injury; then take wool, and soak it in juice of plantain or agrimony with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and what is called "albathir" is red and resembles a hard head, so it must be cut as I have said about the thulul; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	for abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the flesh, such as cankers and stony abscesses and herpes and ulcers and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess which comes in the armpit, which is not of the kind that are found in the bowels; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not hurry to pierce it, but let it die down until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on a chair, and give him two small chairs where he can recline, and support his back and bring his legs together behind the thigh; and keep his thighs spread, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then place the basin towards the right side, and there administer the instrument used to work on the armpit, of which the form follows hereafter; and it is necessary that when you are about to administer this instrument, you insert the point first to know the depth of the armpit, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the armpit with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause pain; and you must place the horn part of the instrument on top, and keep the instrument moist.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is apparent and one opens it by hand gently, then it must be cut at the top, in the spatumile area; and when the pus is emptied out, then you should place in the wound moistened cloths in rose oil or green oil; and put a cloth over the wound and on the bandage linen that is cleaned in water or mulberries cooked; then treat after two days of ointment application as needed, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the bandage and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and yarrow boiled; then return to applying the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed in the bandage, then you must avoid heating with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs thereof when you see a woman press down with her abdomen, and desire to smell the air: then you know that the child hastens to come out; at this point you understand that this birth is according to the natural figure, and its exit is under its head, and the afterbirth comes with it; and when you see these signs, you should gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends by its head, the afterbirth follows with it, and the woman is purified of her superfluities through good cleansing; and those who come out otherwise do not do so naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For there are times when it comes out on its feet, and the body or head faces upward, and the hands come out first, or it emerges above its belly, or behind, and it turns around by chance over its neck, and in other bad positions; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally above its head and the woman gives birth with great difficulty, and if her strength is weak, then let her sit on a chair or stool held by women; and give her something to drink made from oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then place between her two nostrils a small piece of cloth in this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the membrane, and cut it to the nail so that the moisture inside comes out; and press the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then a suppository of fenugreek with sesame oil must be used; then make her sneeze from a mixture of condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: the child will now come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands issue forth forcefully, it is necessary to reset them gradually bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair, and lift her feet upwards; then raise the chair off the ground, and steady the woman so she does not fall when standing up; and if the hand cannot enter, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is placed here beforehand, extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of delivering the child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, it is necessary to lift it up; then turn it gradually bit by bit until it is upright; then take one of its feet and stretch it gradually.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps to the thighs, instruct them to catch it, and make it sneeze from conditi; if it flees further, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go as we have said, turn it little by little until it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it moves lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take muscillage of aloes, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; then place the woman's nature inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to below the ribs; when she is moistened below, apply a poultice of myrrh to her and let it stay for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her abdomen, for now the child will jump.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, place its hands little by little; then support it on its neck, and let the feet hang down, and have it lying on the bed; then bend its hands little by little, and then take hold of its hands above the belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until it is prepared to go down; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them apart, then lift up the belly, then put your hands in; and bring out the child little by little; and instruct the woman to pull herself as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child that comes with one hand hanging out
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary for the midwife to return the hand: if she cannot return it, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie on the bed with her legs straight; then administer the mixture that I have described; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and hold the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to grip firmly until the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the exit of the child upon its neck, and let her spread out her hands, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the midwife to hold the child's hand, then turn it little by little, and place it gently; and when it is even, apply the natural mixture of honey and oil as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little; and when you have done this, have her sit on a chair, and tell her to grip firmly; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for the entire second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to applying force in this manner throughout the second stage, cut the perineum at your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child can pass over its face and neck, cut from the mouth so that it is not held back, and deliver the child; then insert the child as needed, and instruct the woman to push several times: then gently extract.
de l’issue des gemelz	on the outcome of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You should know that twins often come into the world, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, though it does rarely occur.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if one can name them; I know that they multiply, and are separated by the surface which divides them, which is attached to the body; and sometimes they emerge as naturally as other parts, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge severely, treat them as we have said, and let the hand be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do so as is needed for their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or even up to XV, and are completely shaped like a child according to the measurement of the wise sage, and it is necessary for the hand to be careful with all this, because similar things may happen; so do as is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is healthy and has no accident where she fears death; it is necessary that the woman be positioned on her back, and her thighs inclined downward, and her legs raised; then the assistant holds her in two parts, or she lies on the bed so that she is not stretched out during the descent of the child; then rub her mouth with oil mixed with muscillaige of hellebore and fenugreek seeds and flax seed; then apply these oils to her hands and these muscillaiges; then gently put your hand in the oil, and seek one place where you can apply the hooks that are suitable for this purpose, and watch if the child is prepared to descend headfirst; then insert the hook into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or on the forceps or near the sides, and if the descent is by feet, fix it in the heels and at the middle of the ribs; you must hold the hook with your right hand, place the curve between both fingers of your left hand, gently press with your whole hand, and insert the hook into any of these places we have mentioned until it comes out empty; this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert against the other hook, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch it evenly by moving from one side to the other, to make the hooks emerge, and let the hooks be toothed to hold the flesh, as shown in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, anoint the sides with some of the oil, and place it in that part, and draw out the other part; and if there is anything left, place this hook or higher up, and do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and he cannot bring it back for grasping, you must wrap it up on the finger until it all emerges; then cut at the joint of the knuckle or the side, and likewise you must do this with the other hand, and with both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is tight at the birth canal, where there may be a fever gathered in the head, you must insert a spatumile between your two fingers, cut open the head, and extract the fluid; or shave it with an instrument called "almidach," whose shape comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and do likewise if the child has a large head naturally; then pull out the bones with pincers, and if the head remains stuck and is tight against the forceps, cut them as needed until the moisture which is inside the birth canal can come out; and if it cannot come out, cut it piece by piece as much as you can; and if it swells in the belly or beneath the ribs, then you must pierce it until the fluid runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustment to the mouth of the socket is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if he is tight in the belly or breast, then you must stretch him with one hand wrapped in cloth; and cut open the belly or chest until the moisture inside has been released; and if another member has been removed and the head remains, then put your thumb or two fingers into it, and pull firmly; and if the mouth of the socket is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has come there, then you should not work on it, but rather treat with moist and fatty substances; and the treatment as plasters, and seep in water that softens and moisturizes.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it level, then treat it as we have said in the case of a living child; and if one has no power over it, then cut it up piece by piece, and leave nothing of the membrane behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat it as we have said for large abscesses that come with pain; and if blood discharge occurs, put it in water to constrict, and treat it with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom the fetus in her womb had died, and then another was conceived after that one, which also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her throat, and it swelled so much that it burst, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought long about it, and could not stop the bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied an ointment of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, for there are no bones in the belly.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it must be the bone of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I explored the wound and pulled out many bones until the woman was at a much better point; and I tended to the woman for a long time in this way, and she would occasionally discharge some fluid from the area; and I recall this chapter only because when masters find something strange, they should seek help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the form of the traction device, which is used in the books; and for two turns at the two shoulders of the two arms.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be finer than the traction device, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the wood one finger thick, and a length of one palm and a half; and between the two limbs there should be two fittings of this same shaft, which are firmly attached to each other, about half a palm long or slightly more; and these two fittings are inserted into the mouth of the joint to open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony wood or boxwood according to the likeness of pliers; and have at both ends two attachments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; then when you wish to open the fist with all the instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, feet hanging down and legs spread apart, then place the two attachments together in her fist, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand on the whole instrument as you did with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you wish to open the mouth of the fist, until she turns it as she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all designed at the top, and their appearances are varied; and when the doctors have them prepared, they work more quickly with them, and they appear larger to people according to their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument because you have not prepared it, for their need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze forcefully, while holding your hands over her mouth and nose; if she jumps because of this, so much the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in its cover, then place herbs that can open the mouth of the woman giving birth inside it, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, savory, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them should be boiled or cooked in water over the fire; then put one end of a tube into the pot hole, and the other end in the mouth of the woman giving birth, and hold it while steam enters her; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The second joint jumps quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not move as desired, instruct the patient to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or mastic of althaea, and then place it on the affected area, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take hold of it and extend it slowly straight, so that the malady does not fall during extraction; but you must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and dislodge.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the malady is tightly sealed, we have described the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not move despite everything we have said, be careful not to overdo it in pulling; but you must bind what is at the mouth of the malady to the woman's thigh, then give her a clyster of tetrafarmakon ointment; this will purge and reset, and she will recover; however, when it purges if there comes an unpleasant odor to the stomach and head, and discolored the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, appropriate fumigations are necessary for these cases: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain her flowers and second menstruation is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a tube, and place the fine tip inside the body, and the wide end over the fire; and let the fumigation be above the coals, and continue until the material is consumed, and then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, instead it is blocked by a fine membrane: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane at its proper place, and she must not pierce it too sharply, and be careful not to damage the surrounding area; then apply wool soaked in wine and oil, and subsequently treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that he will not stay still, place a chain through the hole, and leave his hands restrained for days, and remove it when the child wants to go to chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this obstruction comes from a sudden closure of a wound or an abscess; then it is necessary to cut that closure: it should be treated as we have said about the chain of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from behind the anus are nodations, and those that come near the anus to exit, or in the space between the two parts, may have one fistula or more; and when this nodation is old, it works, and still retains moisture, either white or subtle blood, and sometimes these fistulas are perforating; they are recognized by what comes out with stool or flatulence when the patient defecates, and perhaps a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and to half the shaft of the penis; and they reach to the knee joint, and to the root of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula penetrates to the fundament, and does not penetrate: it is that you insert your index finger into the fundament, and insert a fine needle of silk or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is curvature, then insert a fine thread of wax or horsehair until you feel the thread or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no discharge, wind, or odor comes from the opening, as we have said: you know that it does not penetrate; therefore hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the urethra, then he urinates through it, and cannot stop it with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it reaches to the joint of the thigh, then the swelling comes up to that place; if there is no tortuosity and pain around the area, then it will become a bone bow immediately, and neither medicine nor binding with ointment helps; and in these perforated fistulas there is no cure except for surgery, and foolish doctors who intervene are in vain.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case that is not perforated and is not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is done with the patient lying on their back; lift the legs up to the thighs, and bend the knees towards the abdomen; then insert a probe of linen or metal if there is tortuosity, until you know where the probe reaches.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should place your index finger there; if you then feel that the tent has pierced through; and where you feel between your finger the surface or flesh, then you know it is perforated; do not work on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can often heal some, but this happens rarely; and the help one gives is to heat the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as was mentioned before; and insert it very hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the fundament; do this twice or three times, until you know that the unhealthy tissues are burned, which look like a feather of a bird; then treat with moistened tents in butter, until the flesh is restored, then cure with an ointment that promotes healing and unites.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus well, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If that cannot be otherwise for him to be well; and if the fistula enters, and does not penetrate up to the bottom which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or fatty tissue between the bottom and the fistula, and you see the fistula in him who has under this covering of the heart; cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward the tent, then apply the cautery afterwards until it reaches the head of the tent; he will be delivered from the tent, which will fall off; then cleanse those corrupted tissues that resemble a bird's feather, and leave none behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood fails you, and it cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or with a hot medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles two good things: that is to say, the healing of the flesh adhered together, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then treat with wet cloths in butter or ground substances, until the wound weeps pus, and let the flesh be burned in the pus; then treat the wound with hot applications of hardening medicines, and these medicines are dried.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the deepest part of the anus and is distant from the body, pierce it there at the anus, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and it is between two tissues or flesh, where it is near to piercing, there must be no hesitation with trust and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it down to the bottom, or if you can place tents and treat as first; do not go too deep so that you do not cut the tissue holding the anus, and let the excretions come there willingly; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut near the anus, either with a tent or another appropriate instrument; then cleanse the damaged flesh in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and to stop the fistula in a part outside the anus: this is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is at the bottom of the foundation near the skin above, take a probe perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert the thread in a curve from I to II, and insert the probe along the entire length of the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perforated in the margin of the foundation inside, then withdraw the thread from that hole, so you place your finger on the foundation; and pull the tip of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and hold them to each other, and leave for one or two days; and tighten it occasionally, until the thread cuts through the tissues between them and they close; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, pierce it in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not proper to make an incision too deep for the displacement and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinous process where one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not so on the other, because one should not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	for hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the anus, like seeds of sesame, and there are small and large ones, and they contain blood; and some are near the anus and at the head of the anus; but those that are farther away have less moisture, and may contain a little yellow water or a little blood, and their color is like flesh. The treatment for those inside the anus is to instruct the patient to sit down so that the hemorrhoids can protrude, and allow the child (the prolapsed tissue) to appear; hurry then, grasp them with forceps if you can hold them by their moisture, or use a finger, cloth, or piece of cotton; pull them out with your two hands, then cut them off, and sprinkle hot powder that serves as cauterizing agent on them; cauterize them as described in the chapter on cautery, then treat them with other methods until they are healed. If the anus cannot protrude, administer a sharp and harsh enema to wash out what is inside the anus so it can come out freely; when this happens, if the hemorrhoids have already come out of the anus, the treatment is easier; grasp them with your fingernail or forceps, cut them off, then treat them as described until they are healed, and beware of cutting with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So it is necessary that you manage the stitching according to this manner: take some twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread from above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and do so loosely; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do this for all others, leaving one to allow the excess blood to flow; then place a foundation with a piece of cloth moistened in rose oil or cerate, and place it as a base, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave them until they excrete, and when they are released, treat them with ointment and other care, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the bowels or base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness of phlegm in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you cut with the point of a spatula or your nail on the surface above it, without letting it moisten; then treat it until it hardens as needed; and if it does not harden, then shave it more vigorously than before, until it bleeds much, and becomes scabby; then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	with trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A flea is a small flat insect that bites very deeply; and sometimes the cold affects it, and one feels it as if dead from trembling, and it spreads throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose's feather or a strong vulture's feather, and place this quill over the swelling until the circles perfectly encircle the swelling; then turn your hand around the entire quill so that you cut all around the swelling, and bury it deep, and dig out the swelling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a wire of iron or steel according to this form, and make it fine below and grooved above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold the hairs in place and press them, And if you wish, cauterize the swelling as described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or sorrel, or of melted silk or barley; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to the needs of those who receive them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are treated in the care of children and those who are weak and suffering should receive small doses.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is as follows, and the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a spacing where the belly is bound as you see, and the end should be perforated; on one side it has two holes, and on the other one; and the belly in which the medicine is placed can be made from an animal bladder or parchment, and should be perforated all around with small holes, leaving one digit of space between each hole, then insert a strong raw thread twisted ten times around or more into these holes, and secure the belly as you would a goat; when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread before clisterizing; this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with a poultice of oil or oak leaf juice, or something similar, then apply it gently; then press the patient with both hands lightly, until he is fully relaxed, then remove the poultice, and lift the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it flow as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, there will be greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer an enema in a case of diarrhea and the medicine comes out quickly, then repeat it until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or an abscess, then let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine enema in which the skin should be stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments with hands and medicines, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are through falling of stones, and cutting with a sword or knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar things; where they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that falls upon the neck, or head, or foot, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from falling stones or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound large, and you suspect the possibility of a hot abscess: then I do immediately cauterize with cephalic treatment if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the dressing be on the opposite side of the injured part; and avoid the patient an excess of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to cauterize, then let his food be light, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the fresh wound that has not been exposed to air, powder which I will mention shortly; and if it becomes inflamed due to exposure, then apply some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then sew them together as I will explain for belly wounds, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered bone, and it is loose, holding only at one point, then cut it away; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as brains and cooked wheat, like porridge, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find on the skin putrefaction that adheres not to the bone, then cut away all the corruption and apply a poultice, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be staunched by medicines, seek out the vessel, and if you find it dislodged, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you put in this powder which seals as soon as the burn has peeled.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.
