And the manner of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and finely powder it, and apply to the wound, and press firmly, until it adheres well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it tightly, and leave it unloosened, unless it swells; for you do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses only charcoal when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the burn has peeled the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, especially in summer, do not put this powder on it; but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey until it discharges pus; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about head fractures hereafter.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference compared to one on the head, but if the neck nerve or artery is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there should be no other treatment than to leave it untreated and not apply anything constricting, for this harms the nerves and makes them retreat; nor place on the wound anything cold, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water mixed with rose oil, and mallow leaves also washed in sweet water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch and bind it with bandages, then treat it until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and infected with pus, then pierce it at the lowest point; and if an artery is cut, causing blood to flow, then open it, tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut or the passage where food goes through is injured, sew the wound on top of the windpipe, but do not touch the throat itself, only realign it according to its natural form; and then bind it appropriately, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until he is healed; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, then graft it; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove them all if you can, but leave those you cannot reach so that the wound may become pus-filled and be drained and its passage cleared; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there is air bubbling out of the wound: you will know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not deep, and fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at first hour, nor bind it for fear the blood might clot deeply and reach the heart, killing the patient; instead apply a drawing ointment, and bandage it twice daily. If you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient rest with the wound covered for three days, or four, or more; this will prevent spasms, heart palpitations, or strangulation of breath; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat her with bandages and other treatments until she is healed; and if she cannot be healed, and you operate, then you know that there is an abscess; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it as you would for someone facing forward; if it is large, suture it; and if it is small, apply powder, and if it is pressed against the bone, and pieces have been severed, then clean the wound, and draw out any loose fibers that are detached; and if they are not detached, let the wound heal by itself, which will ease the extraction of foreign bodies; and for other wounds on other limbs, follow the judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, for which there is an incision of forceps; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because if one does not frequently replace the intestines in place, they will adhere; because the intestines swell quickly when exposed to cold, so they enter less easily, and for this reason it is better to treat smaller wounds, because one can more easily return the intestines to their proper place compared to other II And know that there are four types of abdominal rupture: two common sutures occur in the suturing of the abdomen, and the sutures for other wounds of the body are two other specific ones; yet they are more specifically used with the suturing of the abdomen, and I will explain each one separately.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine comes out, and it is a difficult thing to replace, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in such a manner: wet a sponge or a piece of cloth in hot water only, which you boil with vinegar and cypress and spikenard, and wash the intestine until the swelling subsides; and sometimes use wine that constricts to do this, which is mild to help reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water in which hellebore and mallows have been boiled, for this gradually opens the entrance; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is such that one should not cut unless there is great necessity for it; and here is the tool for making the incision: cut inward into the curvature without going forward, and see here its form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, place them back in their natural position if you have the power to do so, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the back part of the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on their back with their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the front part of the abdomen, raise the head and feet higher than the middle parts; and similarly, if there is a rupture in one of the two sides, ensure that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus should be treated what I say about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds apply what is suitable, then hold a minister in your hands who holds the entire wound with one hand and brings together the edges; this is the common method of suturing, which involves taking one or more needles according to the width of the wound. Leave about an inch from the beginning of the wound, and insert a needle where there is strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin with both ends of the suture, which are inside the skin, until you have pierced it from that part, and bring together the two outer edges of the suture in four places. Then pull double thread around the needle on both sides, then join the two edges of the wound gradually, and leave another inch and insert another needle; tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this according to how many needles you need until the entire wound is closed; let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter properly: thus they should be medium. Do not insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin, so that they do not injure the wound before it heals; then trim the ends of the needles so they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and place small tents or cloths on top of the needle ends to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. This method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because only one or two are needed. The second method of suturing is also common, which involves bringing together both sides of the skin and both ends of the suture on a needle or strong medium thread; when you have pierced these edges all four together, pull back the needle to where you started in the way that clothes are sewn; leave about an inch between each stitch. This method is known by people, and I stitched up a wound someone had in their abdomen, which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and intestines were protruding two palms long, and the wound was deep inside the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the skin straight through, hold the head of the suture where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner part outward; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as tailors do with skins, and leave once the suture on one side, and take it up on the other, until the entire stitching is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galenus describes properly, is as follows: some do it by bringing together the two parts naturally and joining one end of the suture to the other in such a way: insert a needle at the nearest point of the margin, piercing only that spot while leaving the two ends of the suture; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner part through both edges of the suture; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part through two points on the opposite side of the wound margin. This is the most suitable method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galenus says this and some attest that one should suture the abdomen with two needles, each having its own thread; and one should insert one needle from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and note that when the rupture is inside the abdomen, the suturing is more difficult than in other areas of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the flesh has been peeled off, then reset the intestines and sew; then put on a powder to heal flesh, and if the flesh has been peeled off, apply some ointment that is present until the wound drinks in the treatment; then stitch the wound as you would others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, apply old cotton as soon as it begins to discharge pus, twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal limbs, it is necessary to moisten fine wool in warm rose oil or warm olive oil, and apply it around the armpits and below the shoulder blades; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then administer an enema of boiled black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it affects the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is due to the smallness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back in as you would with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned black or dark, then you must ligate the area that is black so that no blood flows from it, because there are veins and arteries; then cut between the ligature, and suspend both ends of it hanging below the wound until they fall out to ease extraction when the spleen falls, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people, as I saw a man pierced in the abdomen with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became infected and turned into a fistula, from which came evacuation and gas; I treated it according to what I could, and did not stop suturing until he was healed, and the flesh closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healing, I feared the patient might have pain in his abdomen; but he had none, and remained in better condition, eating and drinking. And some experienced practitioners said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be treated as follows: take clamps with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the clamp opens its jaws, place it on both lips so that they hold tightly; then cut off the head, and this holds securely so that it cannot come loose, then place another clamp in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is secured; then suture the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head is embedded in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that matches the intestine of an animal as follows: take the tip of this intestinal thread and strip it bare, then twist a thin linen thread around its end, put the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine shut, and pull it tight at the wound; and this method of stitching is not unlike that of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the major intestinal tracts, there is no remedy but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of an abscess wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it begins to discharge, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is deep and enters the body cavity.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a faulty and hard knot, where no pain is felt, and it is also drawn out like a bird’s feather; and sometimes it becomes clear fluid, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times enough; and I have already spoken about in the division of wounds that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, can only be due to one of the IX causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or body; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, that does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much fluid; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine used in treatment was not good; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or due to the nature of the region being slow digestion, late healing, swollen naturally; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medical treatments in that division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I shall make known to you the treatment of fistula which is performed by hand work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and such as come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you wish to know it, take a probe of iron or brass, if the fistula is straight, then insert it; and if the fistula is curved, search it with a delicate probe made of lead, because lead bends around the curvature; and if the fistula has several openings and you cannot properly explore it with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture passes from one opening to another, and clean it; then feel carefully as much as you can, whether there is bone or nerve, and determine its exact position, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when pressing his hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein, or in any of the places I have said, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove all the diseased flesh that is inside; and then cure until it heals, and if the fistula is deep straight ahead, you must cut as deeply as possible, then put wet probes dipped in astringent medicine into it, up to the top of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes any excess material remaining at the bottom; and then apply ointments that heal flesh until it is healed; and if it does not heal through this method, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is diseased by the fistula, remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not trouble the principal members as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove it until all corruption is gone, then treat the wound with healing substances until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns to its previous state, know that you have not reached deep enough: uncover and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the area; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is any small corrupted bone which can be pulled with forceps, remove it with suitable instruments, and if there are many bones, pull them all out without leaving even one; and if the moisture (pus) obstructs you and there is no error or fear, cut away both pus and flesh, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, place on the wound something that will generate putrefaction, and leave until the flesh around the bone is rotten; then they will have more easily the bones. And if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, remove only the corruption until the blackness be all taken away, then restore the wound; and if there is much of the corrupt part coming to the bone marrow, so you must scrape and cut all up to the corruption, and then cure it until it be healed; and I will tell you of a fistula which happened in a man’s leg, that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body, until the matter reached the leg and it swelled with an abscess; there was no reason to let it out for incision. But through their foolishness, the doctors operated on him so much that they opened the abscesses and removed a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared through which all flowed out as pus and moisture from the body. Many doctors treated him for two years without any skill in the art of hands until I was called to see his leg and the medicines that were being used on him, and what was flowing out through the openings with great volume; the young man’s body turned red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that they came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, which was corrupted and perforated; the corruption reached to the inner bone. I removed what appeared to be corrupt bone, thinking there would be no further corruption beyond that which I had taken out; and began to treat the wound with internal medicines over a long period, but it did not heal. Then I started again and cut into the bone as before, finding the corruption continued in the bone, so I removed it, and worked on healing the area; however, I could only cut around a palm's width of the bone, and treated it until all its flesh was gone, then treated it with medicines; and it healed quickly and closed up rapidly, but further work was not necessary except for the patient's weakness, which he could not endure, and because of my fear that he would die.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurs, but he was entirely healthy, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and he was well disposed and had no harm or contraindication at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated as follows: take some linen, and stretch it over the end of the bone that is visible, and have someone hold it taut; and place another piece of coarser linen under the skin covering the bone, and tie it so that you pull the corrupted flesh inward, and expose the flesh where you wish to treat it, so that the dressing does not injure the flesh; and put a splinter or a small plate under the bone to help cut away the corrupted flesh; and one must continue treating until the corruption can be seen and felt no longer, and repeat treatment as necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and it does not appear clearly, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place a coal underneath, and spread the corruption from one side to the other, spreading the flesh along the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint, and suture the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is at the continuation of two joints, there is no remedy but to cut; and if the corruption is at the finger of the hand or foot, it is very serious, yet you must inquire about that corrosion as it appears to you; and purify in all ways possible, but do not let veins or nerves oppose you; know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bone and its appearance, and its thickness and fineness, and its size and smallness, and its hardness; therefore prepare each kind of instrument for each type of work; and know that the task will show you the tool you need based on the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tools you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head may rot from within or due to external causes; and when you have treated that corruption with medicine but it does not improve, then it is necessary to amputate the limb up to where the corrosion begins so that the patient escapes death by this means, or from the greater evil of losing the limb; and the sign of this is that the limb turns black as if burned by fire, and then the rot spreads after the blackness, spreading corruption through each limb until it reaches throughout the body; therefore hasten to amputate, and if it is due to the bite of venomous beasts such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the hand, then amputate it, and do not give it space to spread further.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cover at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, death is certain, and no remedy will be of use except for the quantity of its virtue; and do this in exactly the same way when the corruption reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cover at the next joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut off the entire foot; and if it rises to the leg, cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sewing the limb is that you bind above and below, and extend one minister down from one end, and another up from the other end, and cut away the flesh between the two ligatures by a span wide until the bone is exposed; then cut or sew, and place a piece of linen on each side so that the wound does not touch healthy skin and cause further injury or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the area quickly or apply some powder to constrict it; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in such circumstances: he was afflicted with a blackness that seemed like a burn from fire, which corrosion first appeared on his foot's toe, spreading throughout the entire foot; when the man saw the corruption, he hurried to amputate his foot, and became well; after much time passed, the corrosion returned to his hand's thumb, and it came to me, and I applied things that would cause regression after purifying his body, but could not stop the corruption; and he vowed that I should cut off his hand, but I refused, hoping to cause a regression of the material; and also feared that if I were to amputate his hand, he might die, as his strength was weak; so despairing, he returned home and hurriedly amputated his hand himself, becoming well again; and no other case has been satisfactory for me except in situations where such a different approach is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess appears in the flesh and remains for so long that it collects a great amount of pus; then it bursts and drains, leaving behind a cavity like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as fine linen, not reaching to the bone or nerve, such a condition is called "sinus"; it is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone entirely, it is then called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you should cut around it entirely, just as when it is thin like fine linen; and it does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you trust that the skin will heal and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cleanse it with an enema thus: check if the breast is large, and the pus coming from it has a foul odor, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine made like this: take myrrh, oil, and litharge in equal parts, put them in a container over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take what you need according to your necessity, mix it with water and honey, and give it as an enema to the breast, and hold the passage tightly; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then release it gently while pressing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the foulness removed; sometimes if that medicine is not available, you can use water from ashes: take ash from grapevine wood, pour water over it, strain it, and give it as an enema until you know the breast is well cleansed; if the patient cannot tolerate these remedies or they are unavailable, then give an enema of water mixed with honey and a little litharge powder ground up; or use an enema made from honey and wine mixed together, where honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and wine helps heal the tissue; once you have done this and trust that the breast is well cleansed, give an enema to promote flesh growth: make a diaphoretic plaster with rose oil and in wine; or use some medicines and ointments whose properties I mentioned when talking about ointments; if the passage of the breast is small and the tube cannot enter, then widen it slightly with a metal probe, place a cloth soaked with Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, sew up most of it leaving only one spot where an enema can enter; if the pus passage is above, cut it lower down where there is less pus.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the wound is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate; and if you cannot cut below the breast as you wish, prepare in such a way that the pus runs to the lowest place where it is, for when the wound is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate and if you cannot cut below the breast as you wish, prepare in this manner: so that the pus flows gently downwards, leaving nothing of the pus; then take consolidating medicines to put on the healthy part, and stretch a linen cloth covering all the healthy part; then cut at the forceful place the opening under the breast one more wide than the first, then spread another layer of ointment according to the size of the opening, and place it over the wound opening to lighten the pus, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days; and that which is on the wound opening, remove often to remove the pus, and check if what flows from the pus is venomous or little or moderate, or digestible, or undigestable; and take heed if the patient feels pain or no, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that rises over the wound opening, then know that the breast is healing already, and approach health; and then untie it in the morning, on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom strikes after a long time, do not despair of recovery, for health is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are those to whom delayed treatments of flesh in their wounds are suitable, and others who benefit from the opposite; and if undigested food comes up from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach does not settle; and if the stomach is slow to heal and is prolonged, add medicines that are dry in substance but potent in efficacy, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the last resort medicine; take a diaphoretic ointment made with rose oil and sprinkle it evenly with old wine; then condense it and use it; and the same applies when cooked and thickened honey is used when no diaphoretic ointment is available: take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them, and mix them with honey while it is over the fire; then form a poultice and apply it to the stomach; sometimes administer aristolochia longa and roots of celestial lilies, which are like flour made from fennel and centaury; use simple or compound remedies: grind them into powder and mix with the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the treatment is prolonged and does not heal by this cure, then know that corruption has set in deeply, affecting bones, hard members, or ligaments; treat it as a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarisis is an abscess that arises below the nail of the finger or toe, and sometimes it occurs in other toes; and when it ages and is not attended to, a foul abscess comes forth, running and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it may run completely under it; and corrosion reaches as far as the bone, causing putrid pain, and the head of the toe becomes swollen, and its color turns black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains around the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, causing it to become inflamed and sore, then you should place the blade under the nail that hurts the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away the flesh carefully and lightly, and apply the remaining flesh with hot and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it away and remove it forcefully, for as long as the corrupted part of the bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the bone is damaged, then cut it as described previously, then treat it until it heals; and if it is pierced and there is great pain, then first clean it thoroughly; then carefully cut off the nail with a sharp tool by cutting across the top, and be careful not to cut into the flesh beneath the nail, for this would cause too much pain to the patient; and if such an injury occurs, then apply something that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second joint that sometimes appears in the hands of some people is entirely flesh, and at other times it has bones, and occasionally there is a nail; and some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the origin is in certain cases within the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born with a nodule on the finger do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger may sometimes move; the size of the one that is flesh is so slight, in this manner: measure it from its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat: be careful when cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the back part of the body, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone in one stroke suitable for him, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wound that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the seam so that the edges repair according to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or wet bandages in rose oil, so they do not seal back together; or place between two pieces of fine linen until it is properly sealed, as is required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If tightly bound to one of his hands with the palm, cut off that binding as is appropriate.
des vils	of small pox or pustules
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick and swollen, filled with melancholic superfluities, which occur in many parts of the body; and they happen more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer enemas to him at times, and then treat him with basilic.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw it entirely out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The treatment of the leg is as follows: first warm the patient's leg with hot water very strongly until the thick blood becomes thin, then strip the leg of the patient from above the thigh to below the knee; then cut one vein or two or three veins at a width, then raise and draw out black blood into your hand, from one side to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can bear; and then bind it up, and order him to abstain from food that provokes black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and this is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the leg is as follows: raise the patient's leg, if it has a lot of hair, then put it in a bath, and warm the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, then heat it by the fire, and then cut along the vein from the base of the knee to below the ankle; then work the skin with a scalpel, and strip the vein on each side until it feels hard when pressed; and you can see it is red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then lift the edge underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then gently scrape with another scalpel as you did before; then make another incision or more if necessary, then cut around the ankle joint, then draw and raise it up to the second incision; then lift it piece by piece until all of it comes out, then cut it off; and if you cannot draw it and raise it, put a needle through the entire strong double thread, tie and draw it, place an edge underneath, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; and be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be drawn or raised, which is harmful to the patient; and when you have completely treated it, put wet wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; and care for it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it sharply, but do not cut it off; and pull it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and it does not cut, for it only severs the vein; and it is thickly curved, because if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein originates in the legs, in warm parts where no grass or trees grow, and in dry ground with little moisture; but it may also arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes beneath the skin, as it arises within the body like serpents and worms, growing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very great inflammation in the leg, then it changes places, and the vein begins to come out, as if the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you must wrap it around a piece of cloth one and a half to two fingers wide, tie it, and leave the cloth hanging from the leg; every time a part falls off due to removal, wrap it around the cloth and tie it again. If it is too long, cut some part but do not cut it at its root until it has all come out; for if you cut it, it will enter the flesh, causing abscesses and putrefaction where it was, leading to a bad illness; that's why it must be treated little by little until there is nothing left in the body. Sometimes this vein can be five or ten handspans long when treated, once for me an inch worm came out twenty inches long, and when you cut it, one of its branches or openings will come out completely; ensure all the matter inside is emptied, then apply medicines to prevent putrefaction for a few days, and treat it as you would abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is superficial, especially when it appears in the ankle joint or foot, and there is much perforation, and therefore it often bleeds; treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease," because it often affects buffaloes, and it is small worms that are born between the skin and flesh, and they travel throughout the body moving up and down, and one can feel them well as they move from limb to limb, until they break through the skin where they go, and cause harm; and it is caused by putridity of certain humors, just as worms and serpents and larvae and ascarids come from the intestines; and there is fear of its malice, because when it travels throughout the body, if it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see that it needs to be drained and drawn out, one cannot force it: therefore, you must bind the area above and below with a strong tight bandage, then cut over it and draw it out by force; and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you do not find it, cauterize the spot with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it causes is that it may reach the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, hold firmly below it the eyebrow properly, then cut over it, and draw it out by force; and the patient should use cleansing of the body from medicines that dissolve bad humors and avoid foods that produce putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from gas buildup
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I witnessed it rise as quickly as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a short while later spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm; she then told me that it circled around her body rapidly, just as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner.
