And when the dislocation has occurred, the patient lies down, as we have said about the one who has gout, and bind the limb on the affected leg tightly, and also on the foot; then place two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a torch between the patient's thighs in the middle form; and place moist cloths around, so as not to burn the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the physician places his hand equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press as we have said in the case of gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, and as I have said; and place your hand on the bad angle, then press with the other hand, and extend towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is behind, one should not extend the affected leg downward nor lift it up from the ground, but rather it must be as if the hip were dislocated backward, as we have described in the position of lying on both hips; and he should lie on his back, with the limb extended as we said before, and pressure should be applied to the joint at the table; and it will be complete when the patient extends their legs equally; then bring the thighs together, apply a plaster, and bind them tightly so that the hip does not move; rest for three or four days, then unbind him, and put on another plaster; if you see that they are equal, bind them again as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not hold at the thigh, then you know it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is as follows: make the patient sit upright, extend his leg if he can, place your back against his back, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly; another assistant should straighten his foot so that the knee returns to its place; the sign is that it holds well at the thigh lightly; apply a plaster, and bind the leg to the thigh tightly for three or four days, then loosen it; and do not let the patient work on walking until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not properly set, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is healed
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes completely dislocated, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it feels loose in the area where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only bruised.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you should have the patient sit upright, and hold them firmly by the thigh from one side; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, then twice with your left hand, then stretch it upwards, and forcefully push the foot upwards; do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start over because it will return; and if it cannot return like this, have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a post firmly in the ground between their thighs, and tie ropes around them to secure the patient; then hold one thigh with your hands or a strap, tying it behind the heel; then stretch each side equally, and the post should be steady between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when stretching; then set the dislocation gently into place with your hands, and another helper holds the healthy leg from behind, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, place the plaster and plugs on it, and wrap it tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and be careful with the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, tighten it again; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if they walk before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if painful abscesses occur, you must soothe them as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of both
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two [shoulders] are dislocated, they must be gently extended without effort, and this is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you have the patient sit on a flat place or on a table entirely straight, and put your foot under what appears to be the joint, then press strongly with your foot until it returns; and when they are even, and there is nothing apparent, place under the sole of the foot a board two fingers thick, then firmly stretch it out, and leave it for three days, then undo it; and have it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not long experience, and if you are not compassionate and cautious, not bold; and use at first soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God’s hands if there is no hope of recovery; and when there is hope, now reset the limb to its place so that the hot abscess does not come; and when the limb is in place, minister soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and treat the wound as appropriate with drying ointments; and if along with dislocation there is a fracture and small bones displaced, remove them, and do as we have said for simple diseases; and guard against entering into ways of fear according to what I have said, because it will cost you more according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your arm and your body.
Amen	So be it
